<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c35db005-051e-4ed8-b7a5-dfdefd0e178f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_493359699" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/493359699" />
    <a title="Petra-X" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x"><img alt="Petra-X" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603179398p2/1237196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/493359699?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petra-X" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petra-X" href="/user/show/1237196-petra-x">Petra-X</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780397000654" href="/book/show/1001317.Parnassus_on_Wheels">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petra-X by: </span>
      3131238-judy
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=2013-reviews">2013-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1237196-petra-x?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer493359699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13906358095126032346"><b>This is a pilot for a new feel-good tv series:<br/><br/>Opening Credits:</b> <br/>It is a glorious morning on a deserted track somewhere in the rural Midwest. Rolling on the lane is a long gypsy-type wagon being pulled by a great big horse. On the open seat up front holding the reins is a cheery man of middle years with kind brown eyes who is laughing gently in a conversational kind of way with a fat, rather plain but very jolly lady. They are wearing clothes of the era when cars and wagons shared the roads, 1917.</span>
  <span id="freeText13906358095126032346" style="display:none"><b>This is a pilot for a new feel-good tv series:<br /><br />Opening Credits:</b> <br />It is a glorious morning on a deserted track somewhere in the rural Midwest. Rolling on the lane is a long gypsy-type wagon being pulled by a great big horse. On the open seat up front holding the reins is a cheery man of middle years with kind brown eyes who is laughing gently in a conversational kind of way with a fat, rather plain but very jolly lady. They are wearing clothes of the era when cars and wagons shared the roads, 1917.<br /><br /><b>Introduction:</b><br />The woman and her older brother have been happily managing their isolated farm together until the brother publishes a book and its success makes him uppity in the extreme. While he swans around being famous, she is left at home running the farm. This is seriously annoying her.<br /><br />A travelling salesmen, selling books, comes to her door saying he is not just selling books but also his travelling bookstore. He wonders if her brother, the famous author, be interested in buying it? He wants to leave bookselling to go back to the city to write his book. <br /><br />He shows her his wonderful, magical wagon full of all the necessities for life on the road and shelves and shelves of books. She jumps at the chance and deciding to spend her life savings and take over the business herself. So leaving a note for her brother telling him to look after himself, she closes the front door behind her, jumps on to the seat next to the bookseller and off they go.<br /><br /><b>Further scenes in the first episode</b><br /><br />Much dialogue between the bookseller and the spinster laying out the history of their lives. He is a city man, a professor who wants to write a book. He is passionate about the ability of books to change lives for the better. She's a bit of a disappointed spinster who counts her successes in hens' eggs laid and wholesome loaves baked.<br /><br />Scenes include:<br />1. Making the first sale.<br />2. The caravan being stolen and the bookseller turns out to be handy with his fists.<br />3. Drama over the cheque for payment being cancelled by the pissed-off brother.<br />3. A bank scene, an arrest, and a false imprisonment.<br /><br /><b>The denoument</b><br />Love. The stranger with a get-out-of-jail-free-card. The inevitable marriage and then the final winning over the brother. All say ahhhhh.<br /><br />Can't you just see it? It was just <i>made</i> for tv. The late Mike Landon would have been perfect casting.<br /><br />Brilliant, lovely, heart-warming book. Beautifully-written without any suspense at all. Each rather obvious episode gives warning of what is to come next and the whole thing unfolds in a pastoral, slower-times, comfy, apple-pie kind of way. A nice book to read curled up on the sofa with a cup of tea or a hot toddy to hand and nothing to do for hours and hours.<br /><br /><i>Rewritten 24 August 2013</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13906358095126032346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1347719065" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347719065" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347719065?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/22462780-parnassus-on-wheels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=dated-social-attitudes">dated-social-attitudes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=gutenberg-freebie">gutenberg-freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=oldies-but-goodies">oldies-but-goodies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347719065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17877755054059053990">This is an old-fashioned, sweet novella published in 1917, about a self-described "fat old woman" (she's only 39) who's never done anything but work as a governess and, later, cook and keep house for her bachelor brother, Andrew. Helen is content with her existence until her brother decides to start writing books about the joys of country life (he calls his first book <i>Paradise Regained</i>) and unexpectedly becomes a celebrity author. Suddenly he's a big "literary man," traveling around looking for </span>
  <span id="freeText17877755054059053990" style="display:none">This is an old-fashioned, sweet novella published in 1917, about a self-described "fat old woman" (she's only 39) who's never done anything but work as a governess and, later, cook and keep house for her bachelor brother, Andrew. Helen is content with her existence until her brother decides to start writing books about the joys of country life (he calls his first book <i>Paradise Regained</i>) and unexpectedly becomes a celebrity author. Suddenly he's a big "literary man," traveling around looking for inspiration for his next book, not helping around the farm, and taking Helen completely for granted. When Roger Mifflin, a short, little balding man with a red beard, drives up to her farmhouse in a horse-drawn wagon filled with books, wondering if her brother might be interested in buying Roger out so he can retire and write a book, that is just the last straw for Helen.<br><br>So she buys the book wagon herself. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440604565i/15998662.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Helen writes her brother a flippant good-bye note, and she and Roger take off in Parnassus, the name of the bookmobile. Roger intends to show Helen the ropes for a day and then leave, but it turns out he has a hard time leaving the itinerant bookseller lifestyle behind. Andrew is hopping mad about his sister's shenanigans and is doing his best to throw wrenches into the works. And is that a smidgen of romance in the air?<br><br>The story is told in a folksy voice. It's simple but filled with gentle humor, and with love for books, and life, and the life that books bring to us.<blockquote>A good book ought to have something simple about it. And, like Eve, it ought to come from somewhere near the third rib: there ought to be a heart beating in it. A story that's all forehead doesn't amount to much.</blockquote>Thanks to Dorcas (my source for many lovely old reads) for the heads up on this one! I love friends who find these obscure older books and review them on Goodreads, so I can go grab them for free on Gutenberg.org or somewhere, and read them myself. <br><br>Don't let my 3-star rating put you off if this old-fashioned kind of story sounds good to you. It's not a great novel, but it's a fun little blast from the past. Those are affectionate stars that I gave out here, even if there are only three of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17877755054059053990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13108541902091845113">What is a good book?<br/><br/><i>".…A good book ought to have something simple about it. And, like Eve, it ought to come from somewhere near the third rib; there ought to be a heart beating in it."</i><br/><br/>Check, check and check.<br/><br/>This is a simple, sweet story (160 pages) about a bookstore on wheels called Parnassus, the woman who buys it, and the man who can't quite give it up.<br/><br/>I love the heart in this story. The woman is described as a fat, middle aged spinster who has spent her youth as housekeeper to her bachelor br</span>
  <span id="freeText13108541902091845113" style="display:none">What is a good book?<br /><br /><i>".…A good book ought to have something simple about it. And, like Eve, it ought to come from somewhere near the third rib; there ought to be a heart beating in it."</i><br /><br />Check, check and check.<br /><br />This is a simple, sweet story (160 pages) about a bookstore on wheels called Parnassus, the woman who buys it, and the man who can't quite give it up.<br /><br />I love the heart in this story. The woman is described as a fat, middle aged spinster who has spent her youth as housekeeper to her bachelor brother. She impetuously buys Parnassus to spite him and in turn has an adventure of a lifetime.<br />Parnassus' owner is short and balding, with a red beard. He is kindly yet fiery, lonely and very literate. He stays with her and Parnassus for a few days for training purposes and ends up losing his heart.<br /><br />Parnassus is a bookish escape and an adventure into the beautiful countryside, villages and farms thereabout. Any book lover will appreciate this almost fantasy existence. Who wouldn't love a bookstore on wheels, a bedroom nook inside, cooking over a campfire in the mornings with a faithful dog trailing beside?<br /><br />Read and enjoy<br /><br />CONTENT: Suitable for all readers</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7463947398270714679">I'll admit to being sort of torn on how many stars to give this story. At times I feel like I'm a little too liberal with how I fling 5 stars around at book reviews. In this case, the story wasn't anything so complex. It was just a short, simple adventure vaguely reminiscent of The Adventures of Tom Sawyer if Tom Sawyer had really, really loved books. And been a woman. But I had so much fun reading it that I couldn't put the story down. It was short, sweet, and didn't try to be anything other th</span>
  <span id="freeText7463947398270714679" style="display:none">I'll admit to being sort of torn on how many stars to give this story. At times I feel like I'm a little too liberal with how I fling 5 stars around at book reviews. In this case, the story wasn't anything so complex. It was just a short, simple adventure vaguely reminiscent of The Adventures of Tom Sawyer if Tom Sawyer had really, really loved books. And been a woman. But I had so much fun reading it that I couldn't put the story down. It was short, sweet, and didn't try to be anything other than a fun little book lovers' book. The fact that I'm excited about reading the sequel was enough to push the story up and over the 4 stars that I might have given it for the straightforward story. I loved these characters, and I loved the simplicity, and I couldn't wait to read more. If that's not a 5 star read, then I'm not really sure what is...</span>

<div id="review_1609795990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1609795990" />
    <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens"><img alt="DeB MaRtEnS" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593294620p2/9827967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1609795990?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="DeB MaRtEnS" class="user" itemprop="url" name="DeB MaRtEnS" href="/user/show/9827967-deb-martens">DeB MaRtEnS</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781935554110" href="/book/show/8696930-parnassus-on-wheels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=aplus-2016">aplus-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=memorably-good">memorably-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=quirky-fiction">quirky-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9827967-deb-martens?shelf=love-finds-a-way">love-finds-a-way</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609795990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12917042425554151419">Without Goodreads friends I would never have been introduced to this utterly charming novella, written in 1917. <br/><br/>Perhaps it is less known than other books which we classify as "classics" because Parnassus on Wheels does not bridge adult and children's fiction, as do "Treasure Island" or "Huckleberry Finn". And it certainly isn't a windswept anguished romance, peopled by lovely young women as do the Brönte sisters' ilk. But it certainly stands the test of time, and for that alone, I must award it </span>
  <span id="freeText12917042425554151419" style="display:none">Without Goodreads friends I would never have been introduced to this utterly charming novella, written in 1917. <br /><br />Perhaps it is less known than other books which we classify as "classics" because Parnassus on Wheels does not bridge adult and children's fiction, as do "Treasure Island" or "Huckleberry Finn". And it certainly isn't a windswept anguished romance, peopled by lovely young women as do the Brönte sisters' ilk. But it certainly stands the test of time, and for that alone, I must award it five stars. <br /><br />Think "adventure". "Tom Sawyer" for the middle aged, the unglamorous, the least likely pair that you could hug if you met them in person. And books...a travelling gypsy caravan hauling classics and cookbooks, poetry and philosophy to rural America, where libraries were scarce and thirst for knowledge growing. Add a gentle mare, a friendly dog and descriptions of farm-style, "turn of the century" cooking - well, irresistible of course. <br /><br />The style of writing is definitely formal, reflecting the era, almost prim actually but there are a few humorous earthy remarks easily missed because they too are couched in an indirect style. "By the bones of Hymen!", is a sly exclamation for which I can't find a modern equivalent, but it definitely is meant as an inside joke as the honeymooners make their way to announce themselves, with plenty of shock and awe. <br /><br />There are archaic words, like "saleratus", an unfortunate flavour permeating a hostess' biscuits...which we know as "baking soda"! The language is dated yet endearing and part of the charm of this lovely little tale. <br /><br />"The cultivation of philosophic reflection was a new experience for me."<br />"I was fanciful, I guess, and as romantic as a young hen..."<br /><br />Miss McGill and Mr. Mifflin will be hard to forget. I recommend that you take the time to introduce yourselves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12917042425554151419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2088830326" />
    <a title="britt_brooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1136632-britt-brooke"><img alt="britt_brooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604426033p2/1136632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2088830326?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="britt_brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="britt_brooke" href="/user/show/1136632-britt-brooke">britt_brooke</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2757888-mikki?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2757888-mikki?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416421944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12833567356276466401"><i>"What absurd victims of contrary desires we are! If a man is settled in one place he yearns to wander; when he wanders he yearns to have a home. And yet how bestial is content—all the great things in life are done by discontented people."</i><br/><br/>-- Roger Mifflin of Mifflin's Travelling Parnassus<br/><br/>This is a tale of adventure, and although actual mileage is accrued and county lines are crossed, it's really more a personal journey -- one woman's mission to travel outside her comfort borders. <br/><br/>For the past 15 </span>
  <span id="freeText12833567356276466401" style="display:none"><i>"What absurd victims of contrary desires we are! If a man is settled in one place he yearns to wander; when he wanders he yearns to have a home. And yet how bestial is content—all the great things in life are done by discontented people."</i><br /><br />-- Roger Mifflin of Mifflin's Travelling Parnassus<br /><br />This is a tale of adventure, and although actual mileage is accrued and county lines are crossed, it's really more a personal journey -- one woman's mission to travel outside her comfort borders. <br /><br />For the past 15 years, all had been well in the life of Helen McGill. Having traded in the rigid demands of the city for simpler ways on a farm, she and her brother, Andrew, settled into a comfortable routine tending to the home, land, and animals. The farm was prosperous, but the work left little time for leisure and so the only "literature" to cross the threshold were government agriculture reports and the occasional Sears and Roebuck catalog. Though that was just fine by Helen because as she put it, "I was more concerned with sitting hens than with sonnets" and so they lived a quiet uneventful life and were...content. That is until an unexpected delivery of books arrived on the doorstep and brought her cozy little idyllic world to an end.<br /><br />Parnassus on Wheels is a fun little book about books that can easily be read in a few hours. Though it was somewhat easy to foresee the direction of the plot, the witty dialogue and quotable passages on life and reading and love were more than enough to keep me interested and still reading. The wonderful message in this simple story is that books are capable of opening up whole new worlds in our lives. They are the gateways to adventure and knowledge -- taking us on unexpected journeys to places we might never have known.<br /><br />I'll leave you with a favorite passage: <br /><br /><i>"I think reading a good book makes one modest. When you see the marvelous insight into human nature which a truly great book shows, it is bound to make you feel small—like looking at the Dipper on a clear night, or seeing the winter sunrise when you go out to collect the morning eggs. And anything that makes you feel small is mighty good for you."</i><br /><br />I will be reading its sequel,<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/609284.The_Haunted_Bookshop" title="The Haunted Bookshop by Christopher Morley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Haunted Bookshop</a>, within the next few weeks which takes Helen's story to a bookshop in Brooklyn.<br /><br /><b>3.5</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12833567356276466401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Miss Helen McGill, spinster of 39 years, did not realize how tired she was of keeping house for her brother, until the offer was made to buy the book wagon, Parnassus, and she began to count how many loaves of bread she had made over the years!   <span id="freeText781399650415652636" style="display:none">This was a delightful little treasure! Miss Helen McGill, spinster of 39 years, did not realize how tired she was of keeping house for her brother, until the offer was made to buy the book wagon, Parnassus, and she began to count how many loaves of bread she had made over the years! How Mr. Morley wrote such an early "feminist" book is beyond me but it was well worth the read. <br />Parnassus according to the dictionary: a collection of poems or of elegant literature. Miss McGill and Mr. Mifflin are wonderful characters and their adventures were quite comical. <br />As Mr. Roger Mifflin sums it up " ...when you sell a man a book you don't sell him just twelve ounces of paper and ink and glue-you sell him a whole new life. Love and friendship and humour and ships at sea by night-there's all heaven and earth in a book, a real book I mean. Jiminy! If I were a baker or the butcher or the broom huckster, people would run to he gate when I came by-just waiting for my stuff. And here I go loaded with everlasting salvation-yes, ma'am, salvation for their little stunted minds-and it's hard to make 'em see it. That's what makes it worth while-I'm doing something nobody else from Nazareth, Maine, to Walla Walla, Washington, has ever thought of. It's a new field, but by the bones of Whitman it's worth while. That's what this country needs-more books!!"</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1348329633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17422299378986256121">Ah, delightful story! I read it through in one sitting (it isn't very long) and loved every bit of the tale of Helen, Roger, and Parnassus the bookmobile. Helen is growing deeply tired of tending her brother's affairs when she meets Roger Mifflin, who wants to sell Parnassus so he can go to Brooklyn and write his book in peace. Helen, in a streak of adventure, buys the mobile and sets off to become a bookseller. <br/><br/>I loved the descriptions—Helen is thirty-nine and "heavy" but shows plenty of sense </span>
  <span id="freeText17422299378986256121" style="display:none">Ah, delightful story! I read it through in one sitting (it isn't very long) and loved every bit of the tale of Helen, Roger, and Parnassus the bookmobile. Helen is growing deeply tired of tending her brother's affairs when she meets Roger Mifflin, who wants to sell Parnassus so he can go to Brooklyn and write his book in peace. Helen, in a streak of adventure, buys the mobile and sets off to become a bookseller. <br /><br />I loved the descriptions—Helen is thirty-nine and "heavy" but shows plenty of sense and industry in her new adventure; Mifflin is forty-one, a "slight little man with a red beard" and a deep appreciation for literature. Parnassus is a funny wagon with covered bookshelves on the sides and living quarters inside...<br /><br />Anyway, this is written in first-person y Helen, and her quick observations will soon have you chuckling indeed in enjoyment of this sweet little gem.</span>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Olga by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7438487-olga-godim?shelf=mainstream">mainstream</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer785124133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17917005446944362373">Charming, simply charming! I don’t believe in all my readings over the years I missed this author. I’m totally in love with this short and sweet gem of a novella, published in 1917, almost a hundred years ago. I’m going to read more of Morley. I’m definitely reading the sequel – <i>The Haunted Bookshop</i> – as my 1947 edition of this book has both under one cover.<br/>Despite its low page count, <i>Parnassus on Wheels</i> incorporates two interweaved love stories: a short, poignant romance of two middle-aged, lon</span>
  <span id="freeText17917005446944362373" style="display:none">Charming, simply charming! I don’t believe in all my readings over the years I missed this author. I’m totally in love with this short and sweet gem of a novella, published in 1917, almost a hundred years ago. I’m going to read more of Morley. I’m definitely reading the sequel – <i>The Haunted Bookshop</i> – as my 1947 edition of this book has both under one cover.<br />Despite its low page count, <i>Parnassus on Wheels</i> incorporates two interweaved love stories: a short, poignant romance of two middle-aged, lonely people, falling in love with each other, and a story of a man’s overwhelming love for books. <br />The male protagonist Roger is a 41-year-old bookseller, a reader and a dreamer. He lives in Parnassus, his home and bookshop – a capacious country wagon, stuffed with books. Roger’s life-goal is to disseminate his love of reading to as many people as he could reach. A born salesman in the best meaning of the word, he inspires people by his passion for literature. Wherever he passes – small farms and large towns – he always leaves behind books and newly-converted readers. <br />The female protagonist Helen is a 39-year-old spinster, keeping house for her farmer brother. A no-nonsense, practical lady, she doesn’t have time to read. Her life consists mostly of cooking, cleaning and other farm chores. On a whim, she buys Parnassus from Roger for $400 and embarks on a road trip of her lifetime: to sell books. Along the way, she falls in love with the bookseller. <br />The plot is simple, with no unneeded twists. The heroes just trundle along the country lanes, selling books and chatting, but I couldn’t stop reading and I smiled a lot. The adventures our travelers encounter are small, the obstacles mundane, but the inner lives of Roger and Helen are so huge and beautiful, they shine in the grayness of our humdrum existence: two twinkling stars stretching their rays of light towards each other across America.<br />My only complaint: Roger talks too much, with too many incomprehensible literary allusions, but like Helen, I sometimes tuned him off. <br />Otherwise, the writing is yummy, humorous and clear – a pure joy to read. The book is a hymn to booksellers, all the owners of small independent bookstores. And for the first time in my reading life, which has been quite extensive, I encountered an introduction to a book written not by a scholar or another writer but by a bookseller, Joseph Margolies. Among the quotes below, the quotes I had trouble choosing from so many captivating and insightful passages in the book, a couple belongs to Margolies.<br /><br /><u>From the introduction:</u><br /><br />
  <i>They [these books] should be compulsory reading for all booksellers and especially for those who are beginning to doubt that there is any romance left in the selling of books. <br /><br />The greatest compliment one can pay to the business of bookselling is that although the monetary return is not great so few ever leave it for more remunerative work. Once the virus has entered the system there is not much that can be done to remove it. </i>
 <br /><br />I wonder: does Amazon count as a bookseller? What about big-box chain stores? Anyone there possesses that virus?<br /><br /><u>From the book:</u><br /><br />
  <i>“Lord!” he said, “when you sell a man a book you don’t sell him just twelve ounces of paper and ink and glue—you sell him a whole new life. Love and friendship and humor and ships at sea by night—there’s all heaven and earth in a book, a real book I mean.”<br /><br />He laughed at his own vehemence. “Do you know, it’s comical,” he said. “Even the publishers, the fellows that print the books, can’t see what I’m doing for them … Sometimes I think the publishers know less about books than any one else! I guess that’s natural, though. Most school teachers don’t know much about children.” <br /><br />“Judging by the way you talk,” I said, “you ought to be quite a writer yourself.”<br />“Talkers never write. They go on talking.”<br /><br />There are three ingredients in the good life: learning, earning, and yearning. A man should be learning as he goes; and he should be earning bread for himself and others; and he should be yearning too: yearning to know the unknowable. <br /><br />When God at first made man (says George Herbert) he had a “glass of blessings standing by.” So He pours on man all the blessings in His reservoir: strength, beauty, wisdom, honor, pleasure—and then He refrains from giving him the last of them, which is rest, i.e., contentment. God sees that if man is contented he will never win his way to Him. Let man be restless… </i>
 <br /> <br /><u>Two new funny words for me in this book:</u><br /><br /><b>Bunkum</b> – empty talk <br /><b>Parcheesi</b> – a dice throwing game <br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17917005446944362373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_388204569" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/388204569" />
    <a title="Orsolya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5647191-orsolya"><img alt="Orsolya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603139114p2/5647191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/388204569?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Orsolya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Orsolya" href="/user/show/5647191-orsolya">Orsolya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5647191-orsolya?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5647191-orsolya?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5647191-orsolya?shelf=books-on-books-language-libraries">books-on-books-language-libraries</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388204569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2725822740451125276">Much can be said of our (a collective ‘our’ for those on this site) love for books. Especially when, we even read books <u>on</u> the topic of books. That is precisely a theme in the well-known novella penned by Christopher Morley, “Parnassus on Wheels”. <br/><br/>“Parnassus on Wheels” follows the interaction between a wagon bookseller Roger Mifflin (Houghton-Mifflin, anyone?) and country spinster Helen McGill. Tired of being tied to the farmstead under her brother’s eye (and hoping to prevent her author-brother</span>
  <span id="freeText2725822740451125276" style="display:none">Much can be said of our (a collective ‘our’ for those on this site) love for books. Especially when, we even read books <u>on</u> the topic of books. That is precisely a theme in the well-known novella penned by Christopher Morley, “Parnassus on Wheels”. <br /><br />“Parnassus on Wheels” follows the interaction between a wagon bookseller Roger Mifflin (Houghton-Mifflin, anyone?) and country spinster Helen McGill. Tired of being tied to the farmstead under her brother’s eye (and hoping to prevent her author-brother from continuing to neglect his own farm-work duties); Helen purchases Parnassus and embarks on an adventure with Mifflin to become a roadside bookseller. On the surface, “Parnassus on Wheels” is a half-romance and half human-interest story. Search deeper and the book envelops the topics of morality, character studies, and of course: the world of the written word. <br /><br />Morley’s writing throws the reader into the plot with vivid descriptions and well-formed characters, each having a unique personality and voice. Although seemingly simple; the story is complex and well-written with a steady pace and thought-provoking ideas. One will discover the beauty of books, the way of life by-gone, and the inclination of women to break free of traditional gender-roles. Add some romance and humor, and Morley’s novella becomes quite compelling, indeed. <br /><br />Although “Parnassus on Wheels” was written in 1915; it doesn’t feel outdated as some reviewers have complained. On the contrary, the passion bleeds through the pages and it is quite interesting to compare the literary world of one era to that of modern day. It also helps that the text is historically authentic and raw, adding the historical fiction element. <br /><br />Each of Morley’s characters is likable and believable, feeling natural and sprite. This pushes the novel and creates drama in an otherwise relatively-calm story. Morley knows how to entertain while being realistic. <br /><br />Once the focus of “Parnassus on Wheels” turns to romance, the pace quickens and a bit too much, in fact. The story feels slightly rushed and even a bit silly. Despite this, the reading is still enjoyable even as the ending is too “peachy” and perfect. <br /><br />“Parnassus on Wheels” is a quick (a few hours, max), charming novella which will certainly liven the moods of readers and is recommended for historical fiction fans and bibliophiles. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2725822740451125276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2367252448" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2367252448" />
    <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira"><img alt="Ivonne Rovira" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339470651p2/3803671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2367252448?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ivonne Rovira" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ivonne Rovira" href="/user/show/3803671-ivonne-rovira">Ivonne Rovira</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/39899825-parnassus-on-wheels">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2367252448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2757112594520488528">Christopher Morley’s first novel, first released in 1917, hasn’t aged a bit: It’s still as funny, touching and thought-provoking as it was a century ago. <br/><br/>Spinster Helen McGill has spent most of her life as the unappreciated housekeeper for her impractical brother Andrew, who has made a name — and some money — writing books on the wonders of rural life in New England. When a traveling book peddler named Roger Mifflin arrives with a horse and cart housing a mobile bookstore — dubbed the Parnassus </span>
  <span id="freeText2757112594520488528" style="display:none">Christopher Morley’s first novel, first released in 1917, hasn’t aged a bit: It’s still as funny, touching and thought-provoking as it was a century ago. <br /><br />Spinster Helen McGill has spent most of her life as the unappreciated housekeeper for her impractical brother Andrew, who has made a name — and some money — writing books on the wonders of rural life in New England. When a traveling book peddler named Roger Mifflin arrives with a horse and cart housing a mobile bookstore — dubbed the Parnassus — Helen decides that, for the first time in her 39 years, she will embark on an adventure of her own. <br /><br />The novel goes in a completely different direction than I expected, but I enjoyed every minute and fell completely in love with the feisty Helen McGill. This is my first book by Morley — a Renaissance man who wrote newspaper accounts, novels, essays, poetry and plays — but it won’t be my last.<br /><br />And, if you get a chance to listen to the Audible edition, you’re in for a real treat! Nadia May truly captures Helen McGill.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_933635781" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933635781" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/933635781?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=humour">humour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933635781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12261486171615494491">I was amazed to learn that this delightful novella was written as long ago as 1917. The heroine and narrator, Helen McGill, could be any thoroughly modern woman who becomes fed up keeping house for her brother and takes off on adventures of her own. Helen was 'rescued' by her brother Andrew from a life as a governess to settle down with him on his farm. She is a placid soul who happily washes, tends the chickens, cleans and cooks for 15 years (she calculates that she has baked 6000 loaves of bre</span>
  <span id="freeText12261486171615494491" style="display:none">I was amazed to learn that this delightful novella was written as long ago as 1917. The heroine and narrator, Helen McGill, could be any thoroughly modern woman who becomes fed up keeping house for her brother and takes off on adventures of her own. Helen was 'rescued' by her brother Andrew from a life as a governess to settle down with him on his farm. She is a placid soul who happily washes, tends the chickens, cleans and cooks for 15 years (she calculates that she has baked 6000 loaves of bread in that time) but when Andrew becomes a famous author from writing about their everyday life on the farm and takes to touring the country looking for new things to write about, she begins to feel restless. <br /><br />One day bookseller Roger Mifflin turns up at her door with his 'Parnassus on Wheels', a caravan of sorts full of books. He's been travelling the roads for years, selling books along the way at farms ans small towns but now has a yearning to settle down in the city for a while and thinks Andrew McGill would be just the man to buy his travelling van. To prevent her brother getting his hands on the van and disappearing for even longer periods, Helen decides to buy the van herself and so embarks on a romantic adventure of a lifetime.<br /><br />Roger Mifflin is a real enthusiast of the power of books and soon infects Helen with his love of reading. She has a gentle humour that flavours her narration with rye assides about her brother and Roger's almost missionary zeal. This is a really charming tale, not only of how one plump, middle aged woman breaks out of a rut to take a risk on adventure and find more than she expected but of the power of a good book to enrich peoples lives. <br /><br />One of my favourite quotes from the book sums up Roger's philosophy:<br /><br /><i>"When you sell a man a book you don't just sell him twelve ounces of paper and ink and glue - you sell him a whole new life. Love and friendship and humour and ships that sail at sea by night - there's all heaven and earth in a book, a real book I mean."</i><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12261486171615494491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_946602692" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/946602692" />
    <a title="Chris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1521829-chris"><img alt="Chris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432561615p2/1521829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/946602692?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris" href="/user/show/1521829-chris">Chris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1521829-chris?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1521829-chris?shelf=best-of-2014">best-of-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer946602692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10675235440454415955">This might be the most fun I've had with a book in a long time! "Professor" Mifflin is a book salesman and Parnassus is his book caravan that he takes from farm to farm, spouting the goodness that can be found in books. A sprite little man, I imagined a leprechaun, quick on his feet with a twinkle in his eye and a love for the written word. One day he happens upon Sabine Farm, where he finds Helen McGill, an overweight, nearly 40-year-old woman who cooks and keeps the farm up for her brother And</span>
  <span id="freeText10675235440454415955" style="display:none">This might be the most fun I've had with a book in a long time! "Professor" Mifflin is a book salesman and Parnassus is his book caravan that he takes from farm to farm, spouting the goodness that can be found in books. A sprite little man, I imagined a leprechaun, quick on his feet with a twinkle in his eye and a love for the written word. One day he happens upon Sabine Farm, where he finds Helen McGill, an overweight, nearly 40-year-old woman who cooks and keeps the farm up for her brother Andrew, an author. After baking 6,000 loaves of bread, Helen has had it, so she gives Mr. Mifflin $400 for Parnassus, and decides she's going to take over the reins of this traveling bookstore. <br /><br />At only 142 pages, this was a quick, but fun read with witty dialogue, a fist fight, and a love story---and this took place over only three days--with a nod to great literature. This originally was printed in 1917 and was reprinted in 2010. I'm glad I happened upon it. As the jacket states, it's "not only a charming romantic comedy, but an inspiring ode to a life in books." Indeed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10675235440454415955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6746567535131917442">What fun. I wasn't sure what to expect except that several people whose opinions I respect have enjoyed this book so much. Sometimes it's difficult to believe that I'm reading words written so long ago, I guess because there is a more modern sensibility rising. I love this early 20th century time period more and more.<br/><br/>I encourage all readers and booklovers to come and read about Parnassus on Wheels, the liberation of Miss McGill, the romance of life on the road. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2137227114" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2137227114" />
    <a title="Kaytee Cobb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22299570-kaytee-cobb"><img alt="Kaytee Cobb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537048250p2/22299570.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2137227114?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaytee Cobb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaytee Cobb" href="/user/show/22299570-kaytee-cobb">Kaytee Cobb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22299570-kaytee-cobb?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22299570-kaytee-cobb?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22299570-kaytee-cobb?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22299570-kaytee-cobb?shelf=so-you-want-to-own-a-bookshop">so-you-want-to-own-a-bookshop</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2137227114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16889350203342572593">I love short little books that are easy to read but full of all kinds of happy fun. This is just one of those books! Helen lives on a farm with her brother. She spends plenty of time doing exactly the same thing every day, for 15 years. When a book wagon named Parnassus drives up with an offer to buy, she decides it's time for an adventure and jumps in the driver's seat. Bookish fun ensues, along with a little dose of love. This little novel was just a blast. I loved every second.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3536345543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3536345543" />
    <a title="Megan C." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7032531-megan-c"><img alt="Megan C." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579012852p2/7032531.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Megan C." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan C." href="/user/show/7032531-megan-c">Megan C.</a>

<div id="review_205640452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205640452" />
    <a title="Bev" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5082359-bev"><img alt="Bev" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374365942p2/5082359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205640452?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bev" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bev" href="/user/show/5082359-bev">Bev</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/12532795-parnassus-on-wheels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=was-mine">was-mine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205640452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11870933881603679067">Actually finished this one late last night, so it counts for the last of my Classic Bribe Challenge Reads. Parnassus on Wheels (1917) is the first novel by Christopher Morley. It tells the story of Helen McGill who is getting tired of taking care of her older brother Andrew who has recently become a famous "homespun" author and who is spending less and less time doing the farm chores that are supposed to be his end of the bargain. One day Roger Mifflin, owner of the Parnassus on Wheels traveling</span>
  <span id="freeText11870933881603679067" style="display:none">Actually finished this one late last night, so it counts for the last of my Classic Bribe Challenge Reads. Parnassus on Wheels (1917) is the first novel by Christopher Morley. It tells the story of Helen McGill who is getting tired of taking care of her older brother Andrew who has recently become a famous "homespun" author and who is spending less and less time doing the farm chores that are supposed to be his end of the bargain. One day Roger Mifflin, owner of the Parnassus on Wheels traveling bookshop, shows up at the gate hoping to sell his wares (lock, stock &amp; barrel) to the famous author. That's the last thing Helen wants. Because she knows if Andrew takes off in the bookcart for more adventures to write up he won't show up at the farm for several months. So, she decides to buy it and treat herself to a well-deserved vacation and adventures of her own.<br /><br />This is a light-hearted and charming snapshot of a by-gone era--days when travel by horse and wagon was the norm. Morley's first novel shows all the promise of his later works like Kathleen and The Haunted Bookshop. The cornerstones of light comedy, a bit of adventure and gentle wit are all there. I enjoyed this little adventure with Helen...although I must say that the more fully developed Haunted Bookshop is still my favorite. Roger Mifflin gives us the benefit of some of his wisdom about the importance of books, but not near as much as we will hear in the later book. Over all, a quick, fun read with a dash of romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11870933881603679067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1364439155" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364439155" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/840004-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366583383p2/840004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364439155?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/840004-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781888173567" href="/book/show/861733.Parnassus_On_Wheels">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/840004-nancy?shelf=audiobooks-2015">audiobooks-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/840004-nancy?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/840004-nancy?shelf=new-england">new-england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/840004-nancy?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364439155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11321615404092307149">I might have enjoyed this more had I read rather than listened to it. Much as I love Nadia May, and she does a credible Yankee accent, narration weighed heavily on the book's rather evanescent charms. Just the same, I'll get to the sequel eventually, even though I see it's not nearly so well-liked.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3473321000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3473321000" />
    <a title="Ritika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7866970-ritika"><img alt="Ritika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595389528p2/7866970.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3473321000?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ritika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ritika" href="/user/show/7866970-ritika">Ritika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7866970-ritika?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7866970-ritika?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3473321000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8084122120139848915">I wish I could remember what had originally inspired me to look this book up.<br/><br/>Morley wanted to right a wrong. A writer called once David Grayson wrote a book on a roving adventurer, and possibly took the domestic side of the adventurer's life for granted (I have not read the book but Morley writes a letter to Grayson in the beginning of the book with a gentle remonstration). Morley hence decides to focus on the oft put-upon sister of a similar adventurer, and sends her off for an adventure of her</span>
  <span id="freeText8084122120139848915" style="display:none">I wish I could remember what had originally inspired me to look this book up.<br /><br />Morley wanted to right a wrong. A writer called once David Grayson wrote a book on a roving adventurer, and possibly took the domestic side of the adventurer's life for granted (I have not read the book but Morley writes a letter to Grayson in the beginning of the book with a gentle remonstration). Morley hence decides to focus on the oft put-upon sister of a similar adventurer, and sends her off for an adventure of her own.<br /><br />Did the adventure take place in a few days instead of the month which was promised? Was the ending rather predictable? Would it all make for a fun rom-com?<br /><br />Yes to everything, and yet, this book is such a pleasant, sweet little read. And has paragraphs upon paragraphs where a reader tryies to explain why reading gives him such joy. It has a middle aged, plump woman as the heroine who also finds herself in the wrong sometimes. She has her reasons to be upset with her careless brother, but also learns to appreciate his response to his true calling, and why it does not make him less than. <br /><br />This is a sweet, joyful, unexpected book and it might seem predictable, but also nothing like this exists!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8084122120139848915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9uZDZwuXuxaqnP0Qt7W4672NjFVXc/Dz1NlGy6ecgyk/x1SsdGV/EKJxhtHP6Qw2aOSHuOrecl/jQBrKwNZjRA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PMLqe36hwrwDeTb/HplimoKlRI1AKyJjoeu2Qh/WIjf14/2wAVMGuguUTT5mxdZHV8xPYP2GoM+WcupDeJzCWg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Cuando el silencio de la nieve no sea suficiente para esconderlo, las muertes ya no se detendrán.\n\nUn hombre desnudo y maniatado, con los párpados cosidos con un alambre, ha sido encontrado sumergido en las aguas heladas de una piscina, durante las obras de la estación de esquí Vall de Beau en el Pirineo: la infraestructura más emblemática de la candidatura hispano-francesa para los próximos Juegos Olímpicos de Invierno.\n\nLa subinspectora de homicidios Álex Serra y el teniente de policía francés Jean Cassel serán los encargados de la investigación. Después de un tiempo apartada del cuerpo por un grave incidente en el que Serra disparó a un compañero, sus superiores la envían a las montañas a investigar el caso. Serra creció en un pequeño pueblo de la zona, al otro lado del valle. Nadie como ella conoce aquel lugar.\n\nCon su regreso, se reencuentra con todo aquello que creía haber dejado atrás: una montaña inmisericorde, un entorno opresivo dominado por los secretos y los recuerdos de un pasado que todavía no ha superado. Ahora, además, un asesino inteligente e implacable la pondrá a prueba.\n\nEste será solo el primero de una serie de crímenes que tienen que ver con una historia oculta durante décadas. Published in 1917, Morley\'s first love letter to the traffic in books remains a transporting entertainment. Its sequel, The Haunted Bookshop, finds Mifflin and McGill, now married, ensconced in Brooklyn. The novel\'s rollicking plot provides ample doses of diversion, while allowing more room for Mifflin (and Morley) to expound on the intricacy of the bookseller\'s art.
